## Chapter: Chapter 17: Research Trends in Multi-Scale System Design:



### Introduction



In the ever-evolving field of system design, the concept of multi-scale system design (MuSS) has emerged as a significant area of interest. This chapter, "Research Trends in Multi-Scale System Design," aims to provide an overview of the current research trends in this dynamic field. 



Multi-scale system design is a complex and intricate process that involves the integration of systems operating at different scales. This can range from the micro-level, such as individual components or processes, to the macro-level, such as entire systems or networks. The challenge lies in designing these systems in a way that they can interact seamlessly and efficiently, despite their differing scales.



In recent years, there has been a surge in research focusing on multi-scale system design. This is largely due to the increasing complexity of systems in various fields, from engineering and computer science to biology and physics. The need for more efficient and effective system design methods has never been greater.



This chapter will delve into the latest research trends in multi-scale system design, highlighting the most significant and promising developments. We will explore various methodologies and techniques being employed by researchers, as well as the challenges they face. Furthermore, we will discuss the potential implications of these trends for the future of system design.



As we navigate through this chapter, it is important to remember that the field of multi-scale system design is still in its nascent stages. The research trends we discuss are not definitive, but rather indicative of the direction in which the field is moving. As such, they offer valuable insights for anyone interested in the future of system design.



In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive overview of the current research trends in multi-scale system design. It is our hope that this will serve as a valuable resource for researchers, practitioners, and students alike, providing them with a deeper understanding of this complex and fascinating field.



### Section: 17.1 Research Trend 1: Open Innovation in Multi-Scale System Design



#### 17.1a Understanding the Research Trend



Open innovation is a paradigm that assumes that firms can and should use external ideas as well as internal ideas, and internal and external paths to market, as they look to advance their technology. The central idea behind open innovation is that, in a world of widely distributed knowledge, companies cannot afford to rely entirely on their own research, but should instead buy or license processes or inventions (i.e., patents) from other companies. In addition, internal inventions not being used in a firm's business should be taken outside the company (e.g., through licensing, joint ventures, spin-offs) (Chesbrough, 2003).



In the context of multi-scale system design, open innovation can be seen as a promising research trend. It allows for the integration of diverse knowledge and expertise, which is crucial in designing systems that operate at different scales. This approach can lead to more efficient and effective system design methods, as it leverages the collective intelligence of a wider community of researchers and practitioners.



The work of Bogers et al. (2017) provides a comprehensive overview of the open innovation research landscape. They highlight the established perspectives and emerging themes across different levels of analysis, which can be valuable in understanding how open innovation can be applied to multi-scale system design.



#### 17.1b Challenges and Opportunities



Despite its potential benefits, open innovation in multi-scale system design also presents several challenges. These include issues related to intellectual property rights, the management of collaborations, and the integration of diverse knowledge and expertise. 



However, these challenges also present opportunities for further research. For instance, there is a need for studies that explore effective strategies for managing collaborations in open innovation projects. Similarly, research is needed to understand how to effectively integrate diverse knowledge and expertise in the design of multi-scale systems.



#### 17.1c Future Directions



Looking ahead, open innovation is likely to continue to shape the field of multi-scale system design. As the complexity of systems continues to increase, the need for diverse knowledge and expertise will become even more critical. This will likely drive further research into open innovation strategies and practices.



In conclusion, open innovation represents a significant research trend in multi-scale system design. It offers a promising approach to addressing the challenges of designing systems that operate at different scales, but also presents several challenges that need to be addressed. As such, it represents a rich area for future research.



### References



Chesbrough, H. (2003). Open Innovation: The New Imperative for Creating and Profiting from Technology. Harvard Business School Press.



Bogers, M., Zobel, A-K., Afuah, A., Almirall, E., Brunswicker, S., Dahlander, L., Frederiksen, L., Gawer, A., Gruber, M., Haefliger, S., Hagedoorn, J., Hilgers, D., Laursen, K., Magnusson, M.G., Majchrzak, A., McCarthy, I.P., Moeslein, K.M., Nambisan, S., Piller, F.T., Radziwon, A., Rossi-Lamastra, C., Sims, J. & Ter Wal, A.J. (2017). The open innovation research landscape: Established perspectives and emerging themes across different levels of analysis. Industry & Innovation, 24(1), 8-40.



#### 17.1b Analysis of the Research Trend



The trend of open innovation in multi-scale system design is gaining momentum due to its potential to leverage a wide range of knowledge and expertise. This approach is particularly relevant in the context of multi-scale systems, which inherently require the integration of diverse knowledge domains and technical skills.



The empirical research cycle plays a crucial role in this trend. As Bogers et al. (2017) noted, open innovation involves both the use of external ideas and the externalization of internal ideas. This process aligns with the empirical cycle, which involves the formulation of hypotheses, the collection and analysis of data, and the interpretation of results. In the context of open innovation, this cycle can be seen as a continuous process of knowledge exchange and integration.



The increasing prevalence of open innovation in multi-scale system design is also reflected in the growth of contract research organizations (CROs). These organizations provide a platform for companies to outsource their research and development activities, thereby facilitating open innovation. The increase in R&D spending from 2015 to 2020 (15.5%) indicates a growing recognition of the value of external research collaborations (Industry & Innovation, 24(1), 8-40).



Moreover, the concept of open innovation aligns with the trend towards smart cities. University research labs are developing prototypes for intelligent cities, which are essentially multi-scale systems that integrate various technologies and knowledge domains. This trend further underscores the relevance of open innovation in multi-scale system design.



However, the application of open innovation in multi-scale system design also presents several challenges. These include the management of intellectual property rights, the coordination of collaborations, and the integration of diverse knowledge and expertise. These challenges necessitate further research to develop effective strategies for managing open innovation processes.



In conclusion, the trend of open innovation in multi-scale system design offers promising opportunities for the advancement of technology. However, it also presents challenges that need to be addressed through further research and the development of effective management strategies.



#### 17.1c Lessons Learned from the Research Trend



The research trend of open innovation in multi-scale system design has provided several valuable insights and lessons. 



Firstly, the integration of diverse knowledge domains and technical skills is crucial for the successful implementation of multi-scale systems. This is evident from the increasing prevalence of open innovation in multi-scale system design, as well as the growth of contract research organizations (CROs) that facilitate this integration. 



Secondly, the empirical research cycle plays a pivotal role in open innovation. The continuous process of formulating hypotheses, collecting and analyzing data, and interpreting results aligns with the principles of open innovation. This process facilitates the exchange and integration of knowledge, which is essential for the design and implementation of multi-scale systems.



Thirdly, the trend towards smart cities underscores the relevance of open innovation in multi-scale system design. The development of prototypes for intelligent cities by university research labs demonstrates the potential of integrating various technologies and knowledge domains in multi-scale systems.



However, the application of open innovation in multi-scale system design also presents several challenges. These include the management of intellectual property rights, the coordination of collaborations, and the integration of diverse knowledge and expertise. These challenges highlight the need for further research and development in this area.



Moreover, the research trend has also shed light on the importance of misuse cases in the context of multi-scale system design. Misuse cases can help identify potential security flaws early in the application development process, thereby reducing the impact on the final cost of the project. However, the misuse case concept has not been broadly adopted beyond the academic world, indicating a need for further work to facilitate its broader industrial adoption.



In conclusion, the research trend of open innovation in multi-scale system design has provided valuable insights and lessons, but also highlighted several challenges that need to be addressed. Future research should focus on overcoming these challenges and facilitating the broader adoption of open innovation and misuse cases in the design and implementation of multi-scale systems.



### 17.2 Research Trend 2: Ultra-Large-Scale Systems (ULSS)



#### 17.2a Understanding the Research Trend



Ultra-Large-Scale Systems (ULSS) represent a significant research trend in multi-scale system design. These systems are characterized by their massive scale, complexity, and the integration of numerous subsystems. They are not merely systems or systems of systems, but socio-technical ecosystems that encompass a wide range of elements, including software, hardware, data, people, and processes.



The research trend towards ULSS is driven by the increasing demand for systems that can handle vast amounts of data and complex tasks. These systems are becoming increasingly prevalent in various sectors, including healthcare, transportation, and defense. However, the design and implementation of ULSS present several challenges.



One of the key challenges in ULSS design is the human interaction aspect. As the Northrop report suggests, many problems in complex systems today stem from failures at the individual and organizational level. This highlights the need for research into how people interact with ULSS and how these interactions can be optimized to improve system performance.



Another challenge is the fundamental gaps in our current understanding of software and software development at the scale of ULSS. These gaps present significant impediments to the technically and economically effective achievement of significant gains in core system functionality. Addressing these gaps requires a broad new conception of both the nature of such systems and new ideas for how to develop them.



The research trend towards ULSS also underscores the importance of empirical research in multi-scale system design. The empirical cycle of formulating hypotheses, collecting and analyzing data, and interpreting results is crucial for understanding and addressing the challenges associated with ULSS.



In conclusion, the research trend towards ULSS presents both opportunities and challenges for multi-scale system design. It offers the potential for significant advancements in system functionality and performance, but also requires a new approach to system design and development. This trend highlights the need for further research into ULSS, particularly in the areas of human interaction and software development.



#### 17.2b Analysis of the Research Trend



The research trend towards Ultra-Large-Scale Systems (ULSS) is a reflection of the increasing complexity and scale of modern systems. As we delve deeper into this trend, it becomes apparent that the challenges associated with ULSS are not just technical, but also social and organizational.



The human interaction aspect of ULSS is a significant area of research. As systems grow in size and complexity, the human element becomes increasingly critical. The Northrop report's assertion that many problems in complex systems stem from failures at the individual and organizational level underscores the need for a more in-depth understanding of how people interact with these systems. This involves studying not just the technical aspects of system design, but also the social and organizational dynamics that influence system performance.



The research trend towards ULSS also highlights the importance of empirical research in multi-scale system design. The empirical cycle of formulating hypotheses, collecting and analyzing data, and interpreting results is crucial for understanding and addressing the challenges associated with ULSS. This approach is particularly relevant in the context of ULSS, where the scale and complexity of the systems make it difficult to predict system behavior based on theoretical models alone.



The increasing prevalence of open innovation in the research landscape also has implications for ULSS design. Open innovation, as described by Bogers et al. (2017), involves leveraging external knowledge and resources to drive innovation. This approach can be particularly beneficial in the context of ULSS, where the scale and complexity of the systems often exceed the capabilities of a single organization.



The use of tools like Carrot, an open-source search results clustering engine, can also aid in the design and implementation of ULSS. By automatically clustering small collections of documents into thematic categories, tools like Carrot can help manage the vast amounts of data associated with ULSS and facilitate the identification of patterns and trends.



In conclusion, the research trend towards ULSS presents both opportunities and challenges for multi-scale system design. By leveraging empirical research, open innovation, and advanced tools, we can begin to address these challenges and unlock the full potential of ULSS.



#### 17.2c Lessons Learned from the Research Trend



The research trend towards ULSS has provided several valuable insights that can inform the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. 



Firstly, the human interaction aspect of ULSS has emerged as a critical area of focus. As systems grow in size and complexity, the human element becomes increasingly important. This underscores the need for a holistic approach to system design that considers not just the technical aspects, but also the social and organizational dynamics that influence system performance. 



Secondly, the importance of empirical research in multi-scale system design has been highlighted. The empirical cycle of formulating hypotheses, collecting and analyzing data, and interpreting results is crucial for understanding and addressing the challenges associated with ULSS. This approach is particularly relevant in the context of ULSS, where the scale and complexity of the systems make it difficult to predict system behavior based on theoretical models alone.



Thirdly, the trend towards open innovation has implications for ULSS design. Open innovation involves leveraging external knowledge and resources to drive innovation. This approach can be particularly beneficial in the context of ULSS, where the scale and complexity of the systems often exceed the capabilities of a single organization. 



Lastly, the use of tools like Carrot, an open-source search results clustering engine, can aid in the design and implementation of ULSS. By automatically clustering small collections of documents into thematic categories, Carrot can help manage the vast amounts of information associated with ULSS, making it easier to identify patterns and trends that can inform system design.



In conclusion, the research trend towards ULSS has provided valuable insights that can inform the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. By considering the human interaction aspect, leveraging empirical research, embracing open innovation, and utilizing tools like Carrot, we can better navigate the challenges associated with ULSS and design more effective multi-scale systems.



### 17.3 Research Trend 3: The Rise of Data-Driven Design in Multi-Scale Systems



#### 17.3a Understanding the Research Trend



The third research trend in multi-scale system design is the rise of data-driven design. This trend is characterized by the increasing use of data and analytics in the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. It is driven by the proliferation of data sources and the advancements in data processing technologies, which have made it possible to collect, analyze, and interpret vast amounts of data in real-time.



Data-driven design involves using data to inform decision-making at every stage of the system design process. This includes using data to identify system requirements, to guide the selection of design alternatives, to validate design decisions, and to monitor system performance. The goal is to make design decisions that are grounded in empirical evidence, rather than relying solely on theoretical models or expert judgment.



The rise of data-driven design is reflected in the increasing use of techniques such as machine learning, data mining, and predictive analytics in multi-scale system design. These techniques allow designers to extract insights from large and complex datasets, to identify patterns and trends that may not be apparent through traditional analysis methods, and to make predictions about future system behavior.



The trend towards data-driven design is also evident in the growing interest in "big data" in the field of multi-scale system design. Big data refers to datasets that are too large or complex to be processed by traditional data processing applications. These datasets can provide valuable insights into system behavior, but they also pose significant challenges in terms of data management and analysis.



In the context of multi-scale systems, data-driven design can be particularly beneficial. Due to their scale and complexity, multi-scale systems often exhibit emergent behaviors that are difficult to predict based on theoretical models alone. By leveraging data, designers can gain a deeper understanding of these behaviors, which can inform the design and implementation of more effective and efficient systems.



However, the use of data-driven design in multi-scale systems also raises several important issues. These include the need for robust data management strategies, the challenges associated with data privacy and security, and the ethical implications of using data in system design. These issues will need to be addressed as the trend towards data-driven design continues to evolve. 



In the next section, we will delve deeper into the implications of this research trend for multi-scale system design.



#### 17.3b Analysis of the Research Trend



The rise of data-driven design in multi-scale systems is a significant development in the field, and its impact is evident in various areas of research and application. This trend is not only reshaping the way multi-scale systems are designed and implemented but also opening up new avenues for innovation and discovery.



One of the key drivers of this trend is the increasing availability of large and complex datasets, often referred to as "big data". As noted by Bogers et al. (2017), the open innovation research landscape is increasingly characterized by the use of big data and advanced analytics. This is reflected in the growing number of research outputs that leverage these resources, as evidenced by the over 125 million open access harvested research outputs available through CORE (research service).



The use of big data in multi-scale system design is not without challenges, however. These datasets are often too large or complex to be processed by traditional data processing applications, requiring the use of advanced data processing technologies and techniques. Furthermore, the use of big data raises important issues related to data management and privacy, which must be carefully addressed in the design and implementation of multi-scale systems.



Another key driver of the data-driven design trend is the advancement in data processing technologies. These technologies, including machine learning, data mining, and predictive analytics, enable designers to extract insights from large and complex datasets, identify patterns and trends, and make predictions about future system behavior. This is particularly beneficial in the context of multi-scale systems, which often exhibit emergent behaviors that are difficult to predict.



The rise of data-driven design is also reflected in the increasing R&D spending in this area. As of 2016, there was a 15.5% increase in R&D spending from 2015 to 2020, indicating a growing investment in data-driven design technologies and methodologies.



In conclusion, the rise of data-driven design in multi-scale systems is a significant research trend that is reshaping the field. This trend is driven by the increasing availability of big data and the advancements in data processing technologies, and it presents both opportunities and challenges for researchers and practitioners in the field. As this trend continues to evolve, it will be important to continue to monitor and analyze its impact on multi-scale system design.



#### 17.3c Lessons Learned from the Research Trend



The research trend of data-driven design in multi-scale systems has provided several valuable insights and lessons for the field. These lessons are not only relevant for researchers and practitioners working in the area of multi-scale system design, but also for those in related fields such as data science, machine learning, and information systems.



One of the key lessons learned is the importance of data management and privacy in the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. As noted in the previous section, the use of big data in multi-scale system design raises important issues related to data management and privacy. This underscores the need for robust data governance frameworks and privacy-preserving technologies in multi-scale systems. It also highlights the importance of interdisciplinary collaboration, as addressing these issues requires expertise in areas such as data science, cybersecurity, and law (Bogers et al., 2017).



Another important lesson is the potential of advanced data processing technologies in multi-scale system design. Technologies such as machine learning, data mining, and predictive analytics have proven to be powerful tools for extracting insights from large and complex datasets, identifying patterns and trends, and predicting future system behavior. However, the effective use of these technologies requires a deep understanding of both the technologies themselves and the underlying data. This underscores the need for a strong foundation in data science and machine learning in the field of multi-scale system design.



The research trend also highlights the importance of open innovation in multi-scale system design. As noted by Bogers et al. (2017), the open innovation research landscape is increasingly characterized by the use of big data and advanced analytics. This suggests that the future of multi-scale system design lies in collaborative, open-source approaches that leverage the collective intelligence of the research community.



Finally, the research trend underscores the need for ongoing investment in R&D in the area of data-driven design. As noted in the previous section, there has been a significant increase in R&D spending in this area in recent years. This investment is crucial for driving innovation and discovery in the field, and for ensuring that multi-scale systems continue to evolve in response to changing technological and societal needs.



In conclusion, the research trend of data-driven design in multi-scale systems has provided several valuable lessons for the field. These lessons provide a roadmap for future research and practice in the area of multi-scale system design, and highlight the importance of data management, advanced data processing technologies, open innovation, and ongoing investment in R&D.



### Conclusion



In this chapter, we have explored the latest research trends in Multi-Scale System Design (MuSS). We have seen how the field is rapidly evolving, with new methodologies and technologies being developed to address the unique challenges posed by these complex systems. The integration of different scales, both in time and space, requires innovative approaches that can handle the inherent heterogeneity and complexity of these systems. 



We have also discussed the importance of interdisciplinary collaboration in advancing the field of MuSS. The convergence of different disciplines such as computer science, engineering, physics, and biology is crucial in developing comprehensive and efficient MuSS designs. 



Moreover, we have highlighted the potential of machine learning and artificial intelligence in enhancing the design and implementation of MuSS. These technologies can provide valuable insights and predictive capabilities that can significantly improve the performance and reliability of these systems.



In conclusion, the field of Multi-Scale System Design is a dynamic and exciting area of research. The future promises even more innovative solutions and advancements that will further push the boundaries of what is possible in system design.

## Chapter: Chapter 18: Industry Perspectives on Multi-Scale System Design:



### Introduction



In this chapter, we delve into the industry perspectives on Multi-Scale System Design (MuSS). The world of industry is a dynamic and ever-evolving landscape, where the need for efficient and effective systems is paramount. As such, the application and implementation of MuSS have become increasingly relevant and important. 



The industry's perspective on MuSS is shaped by a variety of factors, including the need for scalability, efficiency, and adaptability. These systems are designed to operate at multiple scales, from the micro-level of individual components to the macro-level of entire systems. This multi-scale approach allows for a high degree of flexibility and adaptability, making it particularly suited to the diverse and changing needs of industry.



However, the implementation of MuSS in industry is not without its challenges. These include the complexity of designing systems that can operate effectively at multiple scales, the need for robust and reliable performance across these scales, and the ongoing need for system optimization and improvement. 



In this chapter, we will explore these and other aspects of the industry's perspective on MuSS. We will examine the benefits and challenges of implementing these systems, as well as the strategies and approaches used to overcome these challenges. We will also look at case studies from various industries, providing real-world examples of how MuSS has been successfully implemented.



This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive overview of the industry's perspective on MuSS, providing valuable insights for those involved in system design and implementation. Whether you are a seasoned professional or a newcomer to the field, this chapter will provide you with a deeper understanding of the role and importance of MuSS in today's industry landscape.



### Section: 18.1 Industry Perspective 1:



#### 18.1a Understanding the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on Multi-Scale System Design (MuSS) is largely influenced by the current trends and challenges in the business environment. One of the key trends shaping this perspective is the concept of open innovation, as discussed by Bogers et al. (2017). Open innovation emphasizes the importance of leveraging external knowledge and resources to drive innovation within the organization. This concept aligns well with the principles of MuSS, which advocate for a system design that can adapt and scale according to the changing needs and resources of the organization.



In the context of MuSS, the open innovation approach can be seen in the way companies are increasingly looking to external partners and suppliers to provide the necessary resources and capabilities to design and implement multi-scale systems. This is reflected in the R=G concept, which advises firms to focus on obtaining access to resources rather than owning them. This approach allows companies to leverage a wide array of resources and capabilities, enabling them to design systems that can operate effectively at multiple scales.



Another key concept shaping the industry perspective on MuSS is the N=1 principle, which emphasizes the importance of individual customer experiences. In the context of MuSS, this principle highlights the need for systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers. This requires a high degree of flexibility and adaptability in system design, which is a key characteristic of multi-scale systems.



The industry perspective on MuSS is also influenced by the ongoing trend towards factory automation. Automated systems are inherently multi-scale, as they need to operate effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. This trend towards automation further underscores the relevance and importance of MuSS in the current industry landscape.



In the following sections, we will delve deeper into these concepts and explore how they shape the industry's approach to MuSS. We will also look at case studies from various industries to provide real-world examples of how these concepts are being applied in practice.



#### 18.1b Analysis of the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on MuSS, as discussed in the previous section, is shaped by several key trends and concepts, including open innovation, the R=G concept, the N=1 principle, and the trend towards factory automation. Each of these elements contributes to the growing importance and relevance of MuSS in the modern business environment.



Open innovation, as discussed by Bogers et al. (2017), is a key driver of the shift towards MuSS. This approach encourages organizations to leverage external knowledge and resources to drive innovation, which aligns well with the principles of MuSS. By adopting an open innovation approach, companies can design and implement multi-scale systems that are adaptable and scalable, capable of responding effectively to changing needs and resources.



The R=G concept, which advises firms to focus on obtaining access to resources rather than owning them, is another key element shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. This concept emphasizes the importance of leveraging a wide array of resources and capabilities, which is a key characteristic of multi-scale systems. By adopting the R=G concept, companies can design systems that can operate effectively at multiple scales, from the micro-level of individual tasks to the macro-level of overall system performance.



The N=1 principle, which emphasizes the importance of individual customer experiences, is another key concept shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. This principle highlights the need for systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers. This requires a high degree of flexibility and adaptability in system design, which is a key characteristic of multi-scale systems.



The ongoing trend towards factory automation is another key factor influencing the industry perspective on MuSS. Automated systems are inherently multi-scale, as they need to operate effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. This trend towards automation further underscores the relevance and importance of MuSS in the modern business environment.



In conclusion, the industry perspective on MuSS is shaped by a variety of trends and concepts, each of which contributes to the growing importance and relevance of this approach in the modern business environment. By understanding and leveraging these trends and concepts, companies can design and implement effective multi-scale systems that can adapt and scale according to changing needs and resources.



#### 18.1c Lessons Learned from the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on MuSS provides valuable insights into the practical application and implementation of multi-scale systems. The lessons learned from this perspective can be instrumental in guiding the design and implementation of MuSS in various industry settings.



One of the key lessons learned is the importance of open innovation in the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. As Bogers et al. (2017) have pointed out, open innovation allows organizations to leverage external knowledge and resources, which can be crucial in designing adaptable and scalable multi-scale systems. This approach can help organizations to effectively respond to changing needs and resources, which is a key characteristic of MuSS.



Another important lesson is the relevance of the R=G concept in the context of MuSS. This concept emphasizes the importance of accessing resources rather than owning them, which aligns well with the principles of multi-scale systems. By adopting this approach, organizations can design systems that can operate effectively at multiple scales, from the micro-level of individual tasks to the macro-level of overall system performance.



The N=1 principle, which emphasizes the importance of individual customer experiences, is another key lesson from the industry perspective. This principle highlights the need for systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers. This requires a high degree of flexibility and adaptability in system design, which is a key characteristic of multi-scale systems.



The trend towards factory automation also provides valuable lessons for the design and implementation of MuSS. Automated systems are inherently multi-scale, as they need to operate effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. This trend underscores the importance of designing systems that can adapt and scale to meet the needs of different levels of operation.



In conclusion, the industry perspective on MuSS provides valuable lessons and insights that can guide the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. By leveraging open innovation, adopting the R=G concept and the N=1 principle, and embracing the trend towards factory automation, organizations can design and implement effective and efficient multi-scale systems.



#### 18.2a Understanding the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on multi-scale system design (MuSS) is shaped by several key trends and concepts, including open innovation, the N=1 and R=G principles, factory automation, and the TRAK architecture perspectives. These concepts provide a framework for understanding how industry is approaching the design and implementation of MuSS.



Open innovation, as discussed by Bogers et al. (2017), is a key trend in the industry. It emphasizes the importance of leveraging external knowledge and resources in the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. This approach allows organizations to adapt and scale their systems to meet changing needs and resources, a key characteristic of MuSS.



The N=1 principle, which focuses on the importance of individual customer experiences, is another key concept in the industry perspective on MuSS. This principle highlights the need for systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers. This requires a high degree of flexibility and adaptability in system design, which is a key characteristic of MuSS.



The R=G principle, which advises firms to focus on obtaining access to resources rather than owning them, is also relevant to the industry perspective on MuSS. This principle aligns well with the principles of multi-scale systems, as it allows organizations to leverage necessary resources to co-create personalized experiences for each customer.



Factory automation is another key trend shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. Automated systems are inherently multi-scale, as they need to operate effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. This trend underscores the importance of designing systems that can adapt and scale to meet changing needs and resources.



Finally, the TRAK architecture perspectives provide a useful framework for understanding the industry perspective on MuSS. TRAK has 5 architecture perspectives, each of which groups together architecture viewpoints and views of an overlapping subject area. These perspectives can be instrumental in guiding the design and implementation of MuSS in various industry settings.



In conclusion, the industry perspective on MuSS is shaped by several key trends and concepts, including open innovation, the N=1 and R=G principles, factory automation, and the TRAK architecture perspectives. Understanding these concepts can provide valuable insights into the practical application and implementation of multi-scale systems.



#### 18.2b Analysis of the Industry Perspective



Analyzing the industry perspective on multi-scale system design (MuSS) reveals a shift towards more open, flexible, and adaptable systems. This shift is driven by the principles of open innovation, N=1, R=G, factory automation, and the TRAK architecture perspectives.



Open innovation, as discussed by Bogers et al. (2017), encourages organizations to leverage external knowledge and resources in the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. This approach allows for the adaptation and scaling of systems to meet changing needs and resources, a key characteristic of MuSS. The open data movement, as described in "Open Data Now", further supports this trend, with organizations like Google, Foursquare, Uber, Waze, Instagram, and Flickr creating products based on freely available data.



The N=1 principle emphasizes the importance of individual customer experiences, highlighting the need for systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers. This principle aligns well with the concept of "smart disclosure" discussed in "Open Data Now", which involves curating information to assist consumers in making purchase decisions.



The R=G principle advises firms to focus on obtaining access to resources rather than owning them. This principle aligns well with the principles of multi-scale systems, as it allows organizations to leverage necessary resources to co-create personalized experiences for each customer. This principle is particularly relevant in the context of factory automation, where access to resources can significantly enhance system performance.



Factory automation is another key trend shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. Automated systems are inherently multi-scale, as they need to operate effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. This trend underscores the importance of designing systems that can adapt and scale to meet changing needs and resources.



The TRAK architecture perspectives provide a useful framework for understanding the industry perspective on MuSS. These perspectives emphasize the importance of understanding the relationships between different elements of a system and the need for systems to be adaptable and scalable.



In conclusion, the industry perspective on MuSS is shaped by a shift towards more open, flexible, and adaptable systems. This shift is driven by several key trends and concepts, including open innovation, the N=1 and R=G principles, factory automation, and the TRAK architecture perspectives. These trends and concepts provide a comprehensive framework for understanding and implementing MuSS in the industry.



#### 18.2c Lessons Learned from the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on multi-scale system design (MuSS) provides valuable insights that can guide the design and implementation of these systems. Here are some key lessons learned:



1. **Open Innovation is Crucial:** As discussed by Bogers et al. (2017), open innovation is a key driver in the shift towards more flexible and adaptable systems. This approach encourages organizations to leverage external knowledge and resources, allowing for the adaptation and scaling of systems to meet changing needs and resources. This is particularly relevant in the context of MuSS, where systems need to be adaptable to different scales and contexts (Ottosson, S).



2. **Individual Customer Experiences Matter:** The N=1 principle emphasizes the importance of individual customer experiences, highlighting the need for systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers. This aligns well with the concept of "smart disclosure", which involves curating information to assist consumers in making purchase decisions.



3. **Access to Resources is More Important than Ownership:** The R=G principle advises firms to focus on obtaining access to resources rather than owning them. This principle aligns well with the principles of multi-scale systems, as it allows organizations to leverage necessary resources to co-create personalized experiences for each customer. This is particularly relevant in the context of factory automation, where access to resources can significantly enhance system performance.



4. **Automation is Key:** Factory automation is another key trend shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. Automated systems are inherently multi-scale, as they need to operate effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. This underscores the importance of designing systems that can adapt to different scales and contexts.



5. **Process Maturity is Essential:** The Capability Maturity Model Integration (CMMI) model provides a useful framework for assessing the maturity of an organization's processes. However, it is important to note that the model mostly deals with "what" processes should be implemented, and not so much with "how" they can be implemented. This suggests that the implementation of MuSS should be guided by a clear understanding of the organization's process maturity and the specific needs and contexts of the organization (SEI, 2002).



In conclusion, the industry perspective on MuSS provides valuable insights that can guide the design and implementation of these systems. By leveraging open innovation, focusing on individual customer experiences, prioritizing access to resources, embracing automation, and understanding process maturity, organizations can design and implement effective multi-scale systems.



#### 18.3a Understanding the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on multi-scale system design (MuSS) is shaped by several key trends and principles. These include the principles of N=1 and R=G, the trend towards factory automation, and the TRAK architecture perspectives. 



The principle of N=1 emphasizes the importance of individual customer experiences. In the context of MuSS, this means designing systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers. This requires a strong focus on analytics, which can help organizations identify trends and unique opportunities, and engage in product co-creation with their customers (Ottosson, S).



The principle of R=G advises firms to focus on obtaining access to resources rather than owning them. This aligns well with the principles of multi-scale systems, as it allows organizations to leverage necessary resources to co-create personalized experiences for each customer. This is particularly relevant in the context of factory automation, where access to resources can significantly enhance system performance.



Factory automation is another key trend shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. Automated systems are inherently multi-scale, as they need to operate effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. This underscores the importance of designing systems that can adapt to different scales and contexts.



The TRAK architecture perspectives provide a useful framework for understanding the industry perspective on MuSS. These perspectives cover the enduring capabilities that are needed as part of the bigger enterprise, as well as the logical view of what is needed in response to these capabilities. This includes the logical connection of nodes, such as a service control centre, to other nodes.



In the following sections, we will delve deeper into these trends and principles, and explore how they can guide the design and implementation of multi-scale systems.



#### 18.3b Analysis of the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on MuSS is largely influenced by the principles of open innovation, factory automation infrastructure, and the utilization of open data. 



Open innovation, as described by Bogers et al. (2017), is a paradigm that assumes that firms can and should use external ideas as well as internal ideas, and internal and external paths to market, as they look to advance their technology. This perspective aligns with the principle of R=G, which encourages firms to focus on obtaining access to resources rather than owning them. In the context of MuSS, open innovation can facilitate the co-creation of personalized experiences for each customer by leveraging external resources and ideas.



Factory automation infrastructure, as described by the kinematic chain principle, is another key trend shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. The kinematic chain principle refers to the sequence of rigid bodies in a mechanical system, connected by joints to form a closed chain or a tree structure. In the context of MuSS, this principle can guide the design of systems that can adapt to different scales and contexts, operating effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance.



The utilization of open data, as discussed in the book "Open Data Now", is another important trend influencing the industry perspective on MuSS. Open data can provide valuable insights into customer behavior and preferences, which can in turn inform the design of multi-scale systems. For instance, GPS open data has been used by companies like Google, Foursquare, Uber, Waze, Instagram, and Flickr to create products that have a basis in their mapping services. This demonstrates the potential of open data to drive innovation and create new business opportunities in the context of MuSS.



In conclusion, the industry perspective on MuSS is shaped by a combination of open innovation, factory automation infrastructure, and the utilization of open data. These trends and principles can guide the design and implementation of multi-scale systems that can adapt and scale to meet the unique needs and preferences of individual customers.



#### 18.3c Lessons Learned from the Industry Perspective



The industry perspective on Multi-Scale System Design (MuSS) provides valuable insights into the practical application of theoretical concepts. The lessons learned from this perspective can guide the design and implementation of MuSS in various industries.



1. **Open Innovation is Key**: The industry perspective underscores the importance of open innovation in the design and implementation of MuSS. As Bogers et al. (2017) noted, firms should leverage both internal and external ideas to advance their technology. This approach can facilitate the co-creation of personalized experiences for customers by leveraging external resources and ideas. Therefore, designers of MuSS should consider incorporating open innovation principles into their design process.



2. **Automation Infrastructure is Crucial**: The kinematic chain principle, which refers to the sequence of rigid bodies in a mechanical system, is a key trend shaping the industry perspective on MuSS. This principle can guide the design of systems that can adapt to different scales and contexts, operating effectively at both the micro-level of individual tasks and the macro-level of overall system performance. Therefore, a robust automation infrastructure is crucial for the successful implementation of MuSS.



3. **Leverage Open Data**: The utilization of open data is another important trend influencing the industry perspective on MuSS. Open data can provide valuable insights into customer behavior and preferences, which can in turn inform the design of multi-scale systems. For instance, GPS open data has been used by companies like Google, Foursquare, Uber, Waze, Instagram, and Flickr to create products that have a basis in their mapping services. This demonstrates the potential of open data to drive innovation and create new business opportunities in the context of MuSS.



4. **Address Semantic Web Challenges**: The Semantic Web presents several challenges, including vastness, vagueness, uncertainty, inconsistency, and deceit. Automated reasoning systems will have to deal with all of these issues to deliver on the promise of the Semantic Web. Therefore, designers of MuSS should consider these challenges when designing their systems and develop strategies to address them.



In conclusion, the industry perspective on MuSS offers valuable lessons that can guide the design and implementation of multi-scale systems. By incorporating open innovation principles, developing a robust automation infrastructure, leveraging open data, and addressing Semantic Web challenges, designers can create effective and efficient MuSS.



### Conclusion



In this chapter, we have explored various industry perspectives on multi-scale system design. We have seen how different sectors have adopted and adapted the principles of MuSS to suit their specific needs and challenges. The diversity of these applications underscores the versatility and robustness of multi-scale system design as a tool for tackling complex problems.



From manufacturing to healthcare, from logistics to energy, the principles of multi-scale system design have proven to be invaluable. They have enabled industries to optimize their operations, improve their products and services, and enhance their competitiveness in the global market. The case studies presented in this chapter have illustrated the practical benefits of implementing MuSS systems, as well as the challenges and pitfalls that need to be avoided.



As we move forward, it is clear that multi-scale system design will continue to play a crucial role in shaping the future of various industries. The ongoing advancements in technology, coupled with the increasing complexity of global challenges, will only heighten the need for effective and efficient multi-scale systems. Therefore, it is imperative for industry professionals to stay abreast of the latest developments in this field and to continually refine their skills in multi-scale system design.
